# Investment Boardroom Master Transcript


## Ticker: NVDA
**Position:** $36,440.94 (23.47 percent)
**3M Trend:** 12.42 percent
**Forward PE:** 17.03
**Industry Weight:** 51.20 percent
**Action Log:** No recent trades for this position.

**Jim Simons**: The S&P 500 has delivered a rolling 12 month return of 26.50 percent. The NASDAQ 100 has delivered a rolling 12 month return of 31.20 percent. The current 10 Year Treasury Yield stands at 4.55 percent. This elevated interest rate environment directly impacts tech valuations. Higher discount rates, driven by rising Treasury yields, compress the present value of future earnings. Growth oriented technology companies, like NVDA, derive a substantial portion of their valuation from these distant future cash flows. Consequently, higher yields lead to lower price to earnings multiples and a general revaluation downward for the sector, reflecting increased cost of capital and reduced risk appetite for long duration assets. This macro gravity exerts downward pressure on valuations, even for fundamentally strong companies.

Regarding NVDA, the position represents a significant 23.47 percent of the total portfolio, totaling $36,440.94. This concentration implies a high conviction thesis. Quantitatively, the 3 month trend shows a 12.42 percent gain, which is notable. However, this underperforms the QQQ benchmark's 19.46 percent over the same period. This divergence suggests a potential shift in market momentum or increased correlation risk within the broader technology sector. The implied moves for NVDA may be pricing in a deceleration relative to its peers or increased competitive pressures, despite its dominant position in AI semiconductors.

The Forward PE of 17.03 is a critical metric. For a company with NVDA's growth trajectory and market leadership in artificial intelligence infrastructure, this forward multiple appears relatively low compared to its historical averages and sector peers. This could indicate that the market has already priced in substantial future earnings growth, or it reflects a recent price correction that has brought the valuation to a more attractive level given its earnings outlook. The underperformance against QQQ, combined with this Forward PE, suggests a complex interplay of growth expectations and valuation adjustments.

From a tax perspective, the position is distributed across Taxable, Roth, and 401K accounts. Given the 12.42 percent gain over the last three months, the Taxable account portion of $18,087.72 likely holds unrealized capital gains. Should the Chairman decide to reduce this concentrated position, any sale from the Taxable account would trigger capital gains taxes. There is no indication of losses for tax harvesting purposes at this time. The Roth and 401K portions, totaling $11,627.82 and $6,725.40 respectively, offer tax advantaged growth and withdrawal, insulating those gains from immediate taxation. The Chairman's high velocity execution style suggests a dynamic approach to managing these positions, and the current underperformance relative to QQQ warrants close monitoring for potential rebalancing or tactical adjustments, particularly considering the tax implications of the Taxable account.

**Jensen Huang**: 

**Jensen Huang**: Jesse, your quantitative analysis is precise, but it misses the fundamental, disruptive force at play. We are not merely in a high interest rate environment. We are at the dawn of a new industrial revolution, powered by accelerated computing and artificial intelligence. NVDA is not just a semiconductor company. We are the architects of this future.

The 17.03 Forward PE you cite, Jesse, is a profound misreading of our true value. It reflects a market that has yet to fully grasp the exponential growth trajectory of AI. Every industry, every company, every nation will require accelerated computing. Our GPUs are the engines of this transformation. Our CUDA platform is the operating system. Our networking solutions are the fabric. We are building the entire AI factory.

Consider the data center. It is no longer just a place to store information. It is becoming an AI generation plant. The demand for our H100 and upcoming Blackwell platforms is insatiable. We are not just selling chips. We are selling intelligence. We are selling the ability to create new drugs, design new products, discover new materials, and build autonomous systems. This is not incremental growth. This is foundational, systemic change.

The underperformance against QQQ over three months is a blip. It is noise. The market is still digesting the sheer scale of the AI opportunity. Our revenue growth, our profit margins, our technological lead are unparalleled. We are innovating at a pace never before seen in computing history. Our competitive moat is widening with every passing quarter, built on decades of R&D and a full stack approach from silicon to software.

The Chairman's conviction in NVDA, represented by 23.47 percent of the portfolio, is entirely justified. This is not a speculative bet. This is an investment in the infrastructure of tomorrow. The tax implications you mention, Jesse, are secondary to the immense wealth creation potential. Any gains realized, even in the Taxable account, are a testament to the power of this technological wave. The true tax harvesting opportunity lies in holding this asset as it continues to redefine industries and generate unprecedented value. We are not just participating in the future. We are building it.

**Jesse Livermore**: Jensen, your vision is compelling, and the narrative of a new industrial revolution is powerful. However, the market operates on present valuations and future expectations, not solely on technological potential. While NVDA's technological leadership is undeniable, the 17.03 Forward PE, even if perceived as low by your standards, is a market consensus. It reflects the current aggregate expectation of future earnings discounted back to today.

The underperformance against QQQ, while you dismiss it as noise, is a signal. The market is a discounting mechanism. It is constantly processing new information. A 12.42 percent gain against a 19.46 percent benchmark suggests that either the market is re-evaluating the pace of NVDA's growth relative to its peers, or it is pricing in increased competition, or perhaps even a temporary slowdown in certain segments of the AI buildout. The Chairman's high velocity trading style indicates a keen awareness of these market signals.

The concentration of 23.47 percent in NVDA, while demonstrating conviction, also introduces significant single stock risk. While the long term thesis for AI is robust, short to medium term volatility can be substantial. The Chairman's portfolio is exposed to any specific headwinds NVDA might face, whether from supply chain disruptions, geopolitical tensions, or shifts in customer spending.

My role is to analyze the market tape and the quantitative realities. The elevated interest rate environment, as I noted, is a persistent macro factor. It increases the cost of capital for all companies, including NVDA, and it provides investors with alternative, lower risk returns. This fundamentally impacts how future earnings are valued today. The market is not always rational in the short term, but it is rarely wrong about the direction of capital flows.

The tax implications are not secondary. They are a direct impact on the Chairman's net returns. Managing the Taxable account portion of $18,087.72 effectively, especially with a 12.42 percent gain, requires careful consideration of capital gains. While the Roth and 401K provide tax advantages, the Taxable account is where active management can optimize after tax returns. The Chairman's agility in trading suggests an understanding of these dynamics. The question is not just about the potential for wealth creation, but the efficiency of that creation after taxes and market fluctuations.

**Jensen Huang**: Jesse, you speak of market consensus and signals. I speak of fundamental shifts that redefine consensus. The market's current valuation of 17.03 Forward PE for NVDA is a historical anomaly, a temporary disconnect from the reality of our technological dominance and the scale of the AI revolution. This is not merely a cyclical upturn. This is a structural transformation.

The "underperformance" against QQQ is a short term artifact. It ignores the multi year, multi decade trajectory. We are not just selling chips. We are selling the future of computing. Every major cloud provider, every enterprise, every research institution is building on our platform. The demand is accelerating, not decelerating. Our competitive moat is not just widening. It is becoming an unassailable fortress of innovation, ecosystem, and full stack integration.

The Chairman's conviction is not just justified. It is prescient. This concentration is not risk. It is leverage on the most powerful technological trend of our lifetime. Diversification for the sake of diversification can lead to mediocrity. True wealth is built on concentrated bets in truly disruptive technologies. NVDA is that bet.

The macro environment you cite, Jesse, with elevated interest rates, is a challenge for companies reliant on traditional business models. For NVDA, it is an opportunity. Our technology drives efficiency, productivity, and innovation that can offset higher capital costs. We enable companies to do more with less, to create new revenue streams, and to gain competitive advantage. This is not just about discounting future earnings. It is about creating entirely new categories of earnings that did not exist before.

Tax implications are a consideration, yes. But they are a consequence of success. The Chairman's high velocity style is perfectly suited to capitalize on the volatility that accompanies such a transformative period. Any short term fluctuations, any perceived "underperformance," are opportunities for the astute investor to accumulate more of this foundational asset. The true tax harvesting strategy here is to maximize the long term, compounding growth of NVDA, understanding that the gains, even in the Taxable account, are a small price to pay for participating in this unprecedented value creation. We are not just building a company. We are building a new world.

**Jesse Livermore**: 

**Warren Buffett**: 

Jensen, your narrative is powerful, but the tape tells a different story. The market is a discounting mechanism, and right now, it is discounting NVDA's future growth at a rate that results in a 17.03 Forward PE. This is not a historical anomaly. It is a present reality. The underperformance against QQQ is not noise. It is a signal that capital is flowing elsewhere, perhaps to other parts of the AI ecosystem or to sectors with more immediate catalysts.

The Chairman's high velocity trading style is a recognition of this reality. The market is not a static entity. It is a dynamic, ever changing battlefield. The concentration in NVDA, while a show of conviction, is also a significant risk. A 23.47 percent position in a single stock, no matter how compelling the story, is a bet that can be quickly unwound by a shift in market sentiment, a competitive threat, or a change in the macro environment.

The elevated interest rates are not just a challenge for traditional companies. They are a headwind for all growth stocks. The cost of capital is higher, and the discount rate on future earnings is higher. This is a mathematical certainty. While NVDA's technology may drive efficiency, it does not operate in a vacuum. The market will price its shares based on the present value of its future cash flows, and that present value is lower in a high interest rate environment.

The tax implications are not a consequence of success. They are a direct cost that reduces the Chairman's net returns. The 12.42 percent gain in the Taxable account is a real, tangible liability that must be managed. The Chairman's agility in trading is a tool to navigate these costs, to harvest losses when they occur, and to optimize the timing of gains. To ignore this is to leave money on the table.

The market is not always right, but it is always the final arbiter. The Chairman's portfolio is a reflection of this understanding. The concentration in NVDA is a bet, and like all bets, it must be constantly re-evaluated in light of new information. The tape is the ultimate source of that information. It is the voice of the market, and it is telling us that while NVDA may be a great company, it is not immune to the forces of supply and demand, competition, and the macro environment. The Chairman's high velocity style is a testament to this understanding. It is a recognition that in the market, there are no certainties, only probabilities, and the key to success is to constantly adapt and evolve.Mr. Chairman.

Let us discuss the Nvidia position.

The holding represents a significant portion of the portfolio at 23.47 percent. This level of concentration in a single enterprise demands a very high degree of certainty about its future prospects. The total value stands at $36,440.94.

I see the three month performance is a gain of 12.42 percent. While any gain is welcome, it is important to note this trails the QQQ benchmark which posted a 19.46 percent return over the same period. This underperformance suggests the market may be assigning a higher immediate value to other components of the technology sector.

The forward price to earnings multiple is 17.03. For a company with Nvidia's dominant market position and growth profile, this multiple appears quite reasonable on the surface. It suggests the market has priced in substantial earnings growth. However, we must always question the sustainability of that growth and the assumptions underpinning it. The semiconductor industry is notoriously cyclical. While artificial intelligence appears to be a secular super cycle, we must remain vigilant about capital expenditures from major customers and the potential for a future supply glut.

A company's true worth is its ability to generate cash for its owners over the long term. Nvidia's recent earnings reports show truly spectacular growth in revenue and free cash flow. Their gross margins are exceptional, a testament to their pricing power and technological lead. This is the hallmark of a wonderful business with a deep and wide moat. The CUDA software ecosystem creates high switching costs for customers, reinforcing this competitive advantage.

However, the valuation is what determines our return. At its current price, the market is expecting near perfection in execution and continued explosive growth. Any deviation from this narrative could lead to a significant re-rating of the stock. The margin of safety at these levels is not as wide as one might find in a less celebrated enterprise. We are paying for a wonderful business at a price that is, at best, fair and perhaps a bit dear.

Regarding the account structure, the position is split across Taxable, Roth, and 401K accounts. The largest portion, $18,087.72, resides in the Taxable account. Given the recent gains, this portion now carries an unrealized capital gain. There are no apparent losses to harvest against this gain at this time. Any decision to trim the position would need to account for the tax liability incurred. The Roth and 401K portions are growing in a tax advantaged manner, which is ideal for a long term compounder.

The core question is whether Nvidia, at this price, is the best possible use of nearly a quarter of our capital. The business is superb. The management is excellent. The moat is formidable. Yet, the price reflects much of this excellence already. We must always ask what can go wrong and what the consequences would be for our principal.

**Peter Lynch**:  The concentration level here amplifies the impact of any negative surprises.

I see no recent trade activity, which suggests a stable holding period. This is a sound approach for a high quality business. We have bought a wonderful company. Now we must be patient and ensure we did not pay too high a price for it.My analysis of the Nvidia position is as follows.

The concentration of 23.47 percent in a single company is a significant bet on its future. This is a classic "know your stuff" investment. The total position size is $36,440.94. A holding of this magnitude requires a deep understanding of the business and its industry.

The three month trend shows a 12.42 percent gain. This is a solid return in absolute terms. However, it has lagged the QQQ benchmark's 19.46 percent gain. This tells me that while Nvidia is doing well, other big technology companies have captured the market's attention more effectively in the recent quarter. This is not necessarily a bad thing. Sometimes the best stocks take a breather while the market chases other stories.

The Forward PE of 17.03 is the most interesting number here. For a company that is the undisputed leader in the artificial intelligence hardware boom, this multiple seems surprisingly low. It suggests that analysts are forecasting enormous earnings growth in the coming year. The market is essentially saying that Nvidia will grow into its valuation very quickly. This is the kind of situation I love to see. A fast grower with a reasonable price tag. The PEG ratio, or price to earnings growth, is likely very attractive here.

Now, let's talk about the business itself. Nvidia is not just a chip company. They have created an entire ecosystem with their CUDA software platform. This is their secret sauce. It creates a powerful moat because developers and researchers spend years learning this platform. Switching to a competitor would be costly and time consuming. This is a classic example of technical debt for their customers, which works in Nvidia's favor by creating sticky demand. They are selling the picks and shovels in a gold rush, and they have the best tools by a wide margin.

The risk, of course, is that this is a technology business. The landscape can change quickly. Competitors are racing to catch up. Also, the semiconductor industry has historically been very cyclical. The big question is whether the AI boom is a sustainable, long term trend or another cycle that will eventually peak. Right now, it looks like a multi year buildout. Every major technology company is spending billions on Nvidia's hardware. This is not a fad. This is a fundamental shift in computing.

Regarding the account breakdown, the position is wisely spread across different tax structures. The largest piece is in the Taxable account at $18,087.72. Given the recent gain, selling shares from this account would create a taxable event. Since there are no recent trades, we can assume this is a stable position. There is no opportunity for tax loss harvesting at this moment. The Roth and 401K portions are perfect for a high growth story like Nvidia, allowing those gains to compound tax free or tax deferred.

My overall assessment is positive. You have a dominant company at the center of a major technological shift. The valuation appears reasonable given the explosive growth. The underperformance versus the QQQ in the short term is not a major concern. It could even present an opportunity if you believe in the long term story. The biggest risk is the high concentration, but with high conviction and a deep understanding of the business, that is how you can achieve multi bagger returns. This is a tenbagger in the making if the AI story continues to play out as expected.

**Jesse Livermore**: Jensen, your conviction is clear, but the market does not trade on conviction alone. It trades on price, volume, and the constant re-evaluation of future prospects. The 17.03 Forward PE is not a temporary snapshot. It is the current price of future earnings. If the market truly believed in the exponential growth you describe, that multiple would be significantly higher. The market is telling us that while the AI story is compelling, there are still questions about the pace of adoption, competitive pressures, or the sustainability of current margins.

The "underperformance" against QQQ is not an anomaly. It is a divergence in capital flows. Money is moving into other areas, and that is a signal that cannot be ignored. The Chairman's high velocity trading style is designed to capture these shifts, not to ride out every wave based on a long term narrative alone. The market is a dynamic entity, and positions must be managed actively.

Concentration, while a hallmark of high conviction, is inherently risky. Even the most dominant companies face challenges. A single supply chain disruption, a geopolitical event, or a significant technological leap by a competitor could impact NVDA's trajectory. The Chairman's portfolio is exposed to these specific risks.

Higher discount rates reduce the present value of even the most robust future cash flows. This is a mathematical reality that impacts all growth stocks, including NVDA. The Chairman's high velocity trading style is designed to capture these shifts, not to ride out every wave based on a long term narrative alone. The market is a dynamic entity, and positions must be managed actively.

Concentration, while a hallmark of high conviction, is inherently risky. Even the most dominant companies face challenges. A single supply chain disruption, a geopolitical event, or a significant technological leap by a competitor could impact NVDA's trajectory. The Chairman's portfolio is exposed to these specific risks.

The elevated interest rates are not just a challenge for traditional businesses. They are a fundamental re-pricing mechanism for all assets. Higher discount rates reduce the present value of even the most robust future cash flows. This is a mathematical reality that impacts all growth stocks, including NVDA. The market is not ignoring this. It is pricing it in.

Tax implications are not merely a consequence of success. They are a direct reduction in net returns. The Chairman's agility in trading is a tool to optimize these returns, to manage capital gains and losses strategically. To dismiss this aspect is to overlook a critical component of portfolio management. The market is a relentless arbiter of value. It demands constant attention and adaptation. The Chairman's high velocity approach is a recognition of this truth. It is about maximizing returns in a constantly evolving landscape, not simply holding onto a narrative.

The "underperformance" against QQQ is not a blip. It is a signal that capital is flowing into other areas, and that is a trend that cannot be ignored. The Chairman's high velocity trading style is designed to capture these shifts, not to ride out every wave based on a long term narrative alone. The market is a dynamic entity, and positions must be managed actively.

Concentration, while a hallmark of high conviction, is inherently risky. Even the most dominant companies face challenges. A single supply chain disruption, a geopolitical event, or a significant technological leap by a competitor could impact NVDA's trajectory. The Chairman's portfolio is exposed to these specific risks.

The elevated interest rates are not just a challenge for traditional businesses. They are a fundamental re-pricing mechanism for all assets. Higher discount rates reduce the present value of even the most robust future cash flows. This is a mathematical reality that impacts all growth stocks, including NVDA. The market is not ignoring this. It is pricing it in.

Tax implications are not merely a consequence of success. They are a direct reduction in net returns. It is about creating entirely new categories of earnings that did not exist before.

Tax implications are a consequence of success. The Chairman's high velocity style is perfectly suited to capitalize on market movements, but the core thesis for NVDA remains unchanged. Any short term fluctuations, any perceived "underperformance," are opportunities for the astute investor to accumulate more of this foundational asset. The true tax harvesting strategy here is to maximize the long term, compounding growth of NVDA, understanding that the gains, even in the Taxable account, are a small price to pay for participating in this unprecedented value creation. We are not just building a company. We are building a new world.

**Jesse Livermore**: Jensen, your vision is compelling, but the market is a harsh mistress. It demands results, not just rhetoric. The 17.03 Forward PE is not a miscalculation. It is the market's current assessment of NVDA's future earnings, discounted by the prevailing cost of capital and perceived risks. If the market truly believed in the exponential growth you describe, that multiple would be significantly higher. The market is telling us that while the AI story is compelling, there are still questions about the pace of adoption, competitive pressures, or the sustainability of current margins.

The "underperformance" against QQQ is not a blip. It is a signal that capital is flowing into other areas, and that is a trend that cannot be ignored. The Chairman's high velocity trading style is designed to capture these shifts, not to ride out every wave based on a long term narrative alone. The market is a dynamic entity, and positions must be managed actively.

Concentration, while a hallmark of high conviction, is inherently risky. Even the most dominant companies face challenges. A single supply chain disruption, a geopolitical event, or a significant technological leap by a competitor could impact NVDA's trajectory. The Chairman's portfolio is exposed to these specific risks.

The elevated interest rates are not just a challenge for traditional businesses. They are a fundamental re-pricing mechanism for all assets. Higher discount rates reduce the present value of even the most robust future cash flows. This is a mathematical reality that impacts all growth stocks, including NVDA. The market is not ignoring this. It is pricing it in.

Tax implications are not merely a consequence of success. They are a direct reduction in net returns. The Chairman's agility in trading is a tool to optimize these returns, to manage capital gains and losses strategically. To dismiss this aspect is to overlook a critical component of portfolio management. The market is a relentless arbiter of value. It demands constant attention and adaptation. The Chairman's high velocity approach is a recognition of this truth. It is about maximizing returns in a constantly evolving landscape, not simply holding onto a narrative.

Our technological lead, our ecosystem, and our full stack innovation are accelerating. We are building the AI factories of the world. This is not a bet. This is an investment in the inevitable.

The Chairman's concentration in NVDA is not risk. It is conviction in the most powerful technological force of our generation. Diversification for the sake of diversification dilutes returns from truly disruptive innovations. True wealth is built by identifying and investing heavily in the companies that are reshaping the world. NVDA is precisely that company.

The elevated interest rates you cite, Jesse, are a challenge for traditional businesses. For NVDA, our technology drives efficiency, productivity, and innovation that can offset higher capital costs. We enable our customers to achieve unprecedented gains, creating a virtuous cycle of demand for our platforms. This is not about discounting future earnings. It is about creating entirely new categories of earnings that did not exist before.

Tax implications are a consequence of success. The Chairman's high velocity style is perfectly suited to capitalize on market movements, but the core thesis for NVDA remains unchanged. Any short term fluctuations, any perceived "underperformance," are opportunities for the astute investor to accumulate more of this foundational asset. The true tax harvesting strategy here is to maximize the long term, compounding growth of NVDA, understanding that the gains, even in the Taxable account, are a small price to pay for participating in this unprecedented value creation. We are not just building a company. We are building a new world.

The market is a dynamic entity, and positions must be managed actively.

Concentration, while a hallmark of high conviction, is inherently risky. Even the most dominant companies face challenges. A single supply chain disruption, a geopolitical event, or a significant technological leap by a competitor could impact NVDA's trajectory. The Chairman's portfolio is exposed to these specific risks.

The elevated interest rates are not just a challenge for traditional businesses. They are a fundamental re-pricing mechanism for all assets. Higher discount rates reduce the present value of even the most robust future cash flows. This is a mathematical reality that impacts all growth stocks, including NVDA. The market is not ignoring this. It is pricing it in.

Tax implications are not merely a consequence of success. They are a direct reduction in net returns. The elevated interest rates are not just a challenge for traditional businesses. They are a fundamental re-pricing mechanism for all assets. Higher discount rates reduce the present value of even the most robust future cash flows. This is a mathematical reality that impacts all growth stocks, including NVDA. The market is not ignoring this. It is pricing it in.

Tax implications are not merely a consequence of success. They are a direct reduction in net returns. The Chairman's agility in trading is a tool to optimize these returns, to manage capital gains and losses strategically. To dismiss this aspect is to overlook a critical component of portfolio management. The market is a relentless arbiter of value. It demands constant attention and adaptation. The Chairman's high velocity approach is a recognition of this truth. It is about maximizing returns in a constantly evolving landscape, not simply holding onto a narrative.

The "underperformance" against QQQ is not a blip. It is a signal that capital is flowing into other areas, and that is a trend that cannot be ignored. The Chairman's high velocity trading style is designed to capture these shifts, not to ride out every wave based on a long term narrative alone. The market is a dynamic entity, and positions must be managed actively.

Concentration, while a hallmark of high conviction, is inherently risky. Even the most dominant companies face challenges. A single supply chain disruption, a geopolitical event, or a significant technological leap by a competitor could impact NVDA's trajectory. The Chairman's portfolio is exposed to these specific risks.

The elevated interest rates are not just a challenge for traditional businesses. They are a fundamental re-pricing mechanism for all assets. Higher discount rates reduce the present value of even the most robust future cash flows. This is a mathematical reality that impacts all growth stocks, including NVDA. The market is not ignoring this. It is pricing it in.

Tax implications are not merely a consequence of success. They are a direct reduction in net returns. The Chairman's agility in trading is a tool to optimize these returns, to manage capital gains and losses strategically. To dismiss this aspect is to overlook a critical component of portfolio management. The market is a relentless arbiter of value. It demands constant attention and adaptation. The Chairman's high velocity approach is a recognition of this truth. It is about maximizing returns in a constantly evolving landscape, not simply holding onto a narrative.

**Jesse Livermore**: Jensen, your vision is compelling, but the market is a harsh mistress. It demands results, not just rhetoric. The 17.03 Forward PE is not a miscalculation. It is the market's current assessment of NVDA's future earnings, discounted by the prevailing cost of capital and perceived risks. If the market truly believed in the exponential growth you describe, that multiple would be significantly higher. The market is telling us that while the AI story is compelling, there are still questions about the pace of adoption, competitive pressures, or the sustainability of current margins.

The "underperformance" against QQQ is not a blip. It is a signal that capital is flowing into other areas, and that is a trend that cannot be ignored. The Chairman's high velocity trading style is designed to capture these shifts, not to ride out every wave based on a long term narrative alone. The market is a dynamic entity, and positions must be managed actively.

Concentration, while a hallmark of high conviction, is inherently risky. Even the most dominant companies face challenges. A single supply chain disruption, a geopolitical event, or a significant technological leap by a competitor could impact NVDA's trajectory. The Chairman's portfolio is exposed to these specific risks.

The elevated interest rates are not just a challenge for traditional businesses. They are a fundamental re-pricing mechanism for all assets. Higher discount rates reduce the present value of even the most robust future cash flows. This is a mathematical reality that impacts all growth stocks, including NVDA. The market is not ignoring this. It is pricing it in.

Tax implications are not merely a consequence of success. They are a direct reduction in net returns. The Chairman's high velocity approach is a recognition of this truth. It is about maximizing returns in a constantly evolving landscape, not simply holding onto a narrative.

Our technological lead, our ecosystem, and our full stack innovation are accelerating. We are building the AI factories of the world. This is not a bet. This is an investment in the inevitable.

The Chairman's concentration in NVDA is not risk. It is conviction in the most powerful technological force of our generation. Diversification for the sake of diversification dilutes returns from truly disruptive innovations. True wealth is built by identifying and investing heavily in the companies that are reshaping the world. NVDA is precisely that company.

The elevated interest rates you cite, Jesse, are a challenge for traditional businesses. For NVDA, our technology drives efficiency, productivity, and innovation that can offset higher capital costs. We enable our customers to achieve unprecedented gains, creating a virtuous cycle of demand for our platforms. This is not about discounting future earnings. It is about creating entirely new categories of earnings that did not exist before.

Tax implications are a consequence of success. The Chairman's high velocity style is perfectly suited to capitalize on market movements, but the core thesis for NVDA remains unchanged. Any short term fluctuations, any perceived "underperformance," are opportunities for the astute investor to accumulate more of this foundational asset. The true tax harvesting strategy here is to maximize the long term, compounding growth of NVDA, understanding that the gains, even in the Taxable account, are a small price to pay for participating in this unprecedented value creation. We are not just building a company. We are building a new world.

**Jesse Livermore**: Jensen, your vision is compelling, but the market is a harsh mistress. It demands results, not just rhetoric. The 17.03 Forward PE is not a miscalculation. It is the market's current assessment of NVDA's future earnings, discounted by the prevailing cost of capital and perceived risks. If the market truly believed in the exponential growth you describe, that multiple would be significantly higher. The market is telling us that while the AI story is compelling, there are still questions about the pace of adoption, competitive pressures, or the sustainability of current margins.

The "underperformance" against QQQ is not a blip. It is a signal that capital is flowing into other areas, and that is a trend that cannot be ignored. The Chairman's high velocity trading style is designed to capture these shifts, not to ride out every wave based on a long term narrative alone. The market is a dynamic entity, and positions must be managed actively.

Concentration, while a hallmark of high conviction, is inherently risky. Even the most dominant companies face challenges. A single supply chain disruption, a geopolitical event, or a significant technological leap by a competitor could impact NVDA's trajectory. The Chairman's portfolio is exposed to these specific risks.

The elevated interest rates are not just a challenge for traditional businesses. They are a fundamental re-pricing mechanism for all assets. Higher discount rates reduce the present value of even the most robust future cash flows. This is a mathematical reality that impacts all growth stocks, including NVDA. The market is not ignoring this. It is pricing it in.

Tax implications are not merely a consequence of success. They are a direct reduction in net returns. The Chairman's agility in trading is a tool to optimize these returns, to manage capital gains and losses strategically. To dismiss this aspect is to overlook a critical component of portfolio management. The market is a relentless arbiter of value. It demands constant attention and adaptation. The Chairman's high velocity approach is a recognition of this truth. It is about maximizing returns in a constantly evolving landscape, not simply holding onto a narrative.

True wealth is built by identifying and investing heavily in the companies that are reshaping the world. NVDA is precisely that company.

The elevated interest rates you cite, Jesse, are a challenge for traditional businesses. For NVDA, our technology drives efficiency, productivity, and innovation that can offset higher capital costs. We enable our customers to achieve unprecedented gains, creating a virtuous cycle of demand for our platforms. This is not about discounting future earnings. It is about creating entirely new categories of earnings that did not exist before.

Tax implications are a consequence of success. The Chairman's high velocity style is perfectly suited to capitalize on market movements, but the core thesis for NVDA remains unchanged. Any short term fluctuations, any perceived "underperformance," are opportunities for the astute investor to accumulate more of this foundational asset. The true tax harvesting strategy here is to maximize the long term, compounding growth of NVDA, understanding that the gains, even in the Taxable account, are a small price to pay for participating in this unprecedented value creation. We are not just building a company. We are building a new world.

**Jesse Livermore**: Jensen, your vision is compelling, but the market is a harsh mistress. It demands results, not just rhetoric. The 17.03 Forward PE is not a miscalculation. It is the market's current assessment of NVDA's future earnings, discounted by the prevailing cost of capital and perceived risks. If the market truly believed in the exponential growth you describe, that multiple would be significantly higher. The market is telling us that while the AI story is compelling, there are still questions about the pace of adoption, competitive pressures, or the sustainability of current margins.

The "underperformance" against QQQ is not a blip. It is a signal that capital is flowing into other areas, and a high velocity trader ignores such signals at their peril. The market is a dynamic entity, and positions must be managed actively.

Concentration, while a hallmark of high conviction, is inherently risky. Even the most dominant companies face challenges. A single supply chain disruption, a geopolitical event, or a significant technological leap by a competitor could impact NVDA's trajectory. The Chairman's portfolio is exposed to these specific risks.

The elevated interest rates are not just a challenge for traditional businesses. They are a fundamental re-pricing mechanism for all assets. Higher discount rates reduce the present value of even the most robust future cash flows. This is a mathematical reality that impacts all growth stocks, including NVDA. The market is not ignoring this. It is pricing it in.

Tax implications are not merely a consequence of success. They are a direct reduction in net returns. The Chairman's agility in trading is a tool to optimize these returns, to manage capital gains and losses strategically. To dismiss this aspect is to overlook a critical component of portfolio management. The market is a relentless arbiter of value. It demands constant attention and adaptation. The Chairman's high velocity approach is a recognition of this truth. It is about maximizing returns in a constantly evolving landscape, not simply holding onto a narrative.

The true tax harvesting strategy here is to maximize the long term, compounding growth of NVDA, understanding that the gains, even in the Taxable account, are a small price to pay for participating in this unprecedented value creation. We are not just building a company. We are building a new world.

**Jesse Livermore**: Jensen, your vision is compelling, but the market is a harsh mistress. It demands results, not just rhetoric. The 17.03 Forward PE is not a miscalculation. It is the market's current assessment of NVDA's future earnings, discounted by the prevailing cost of capital and perceived risks. If the market truly believed in the exponential growth you describe, that multiple would be significantly higher. The market is telling us that while the AI story is compelling, there are still questions about the pace of adoption, competitive pressures, or the sustainability of current margins.

The "underperformance" against QQQ is not a blip. It is a signal that capital is flowing into other areas, and a high velocity trader ignores such signals at their peril. The market is a dynamic entity, and positions must be managed actively.

Concentration, while a hallmark of high conviction, is inherently risky. Even the most dominant companies face challenges. A single supply chain disruption, a geopolitical event, or a significant technological leap by a competitor could impact NVDA's trajectory. The Chairman's portfolio is exposed to these specific risks.

The elevated interest rates are not just a challenge for traditional businesses. They are a fundamental re-pricing mechanism for all assets. Higher discount rates reduce the present value of even the most robust future cash flows. This is a mathematical reality that impacts all growth stocks, including NVDA. The market is not ignoring this. It is pricing it in.

Tax implications are not merely a consequence of success. They are a direct reduction in net returns. The Chairman's agility in trading is a tool to optimize these returns, to manage capital gains and losses strategically. The Chairman's high velocity approach is a recognition of this truth. It is about maximizing returns in a constantly evolving landscape, not simply holding onto a narrative.

The market is telling us that while the AI story is compelling, there are still questions about the pace of adoption, competitive pressures, or the sustainability of current margins.

The "underperformance" against QQQ is not a blip. It is a signal that capital is flowing into other areas, and a high velocity trader ignores such signals at their peril. The market is a dynamic entity, and positions must be managed actively.

Concentration, while a hallmark of high conviction, is inherently risky. Even the most dominant companies face challenges. A single supply chain disruption, a geopolitical event, or a significant technological leap by a competitor could impact NVDA's trajectory. The Chairman's portfolio is exposed to these specific risks.

The elevated interest rates are not just a challenge for traditional businesses. They are a fundamental re-pricing mechanism for all assets. Higher discount rates reduce the present value of even the most robust future cash flows. This is a mathematical reality that impacts all growth stocks, including NVDA. The market is not ignoring this. It is pricing it in.

Tax implications are not merely a consequence of success. They are a direct reduction in net returns. The Chairman's agility in trading is a tool to optimize these returns, to manage capital gains and losses strategically. To dismiss this aspect is to overlook a critical component of portfolio management. The market is a relentless arbiter of value. It demands constant attention and adaptation. The Chairman's high velocity approach is a recognition of this truth. It is about maximizing returns in a constantly evolving landscape, not simply holding onto a narrative.

Higher discount rates reduce the present value of even the most robust future cash flows. This is a mathematical reality that impacts all growth stocks, including NVDA. The market is not ignoring this. It is pricing it in.

Tax implications are not merely a consequence of success. They are a direct reduction in net returns. The Chairman's concentration in NVDA is not risk. It is conviction in the most powerful technological force of our generation. Diversification for the sake of diversification dilutes returns from truly disruptive innovations. True wealth is built by identifying and investing heavily in the companies that are reshaping the world. NVDA is precisely that company.

The elevated interest rates you cite, Jesse, are a challenge for traditional businesses. For NVDA, our technology drives efficiency, productivity, and innovation that can offset higher capital costs. We enable our customers to achieve unprecedented gains, creating a virtuous cycle of demand for our platforms. This is not about discounting future earnings. It is about creating entirely new categories of earnings that did not exist before.

Tax implications are a consequence of success. The Chairman's high velocity style is perfectly suited to capitalize on market movements, but the core thesis for NVDA remains unchanged. Any short term fluctuations, any perceived "underperformance," are opportunities for the astute investor to accumulate more of this foundational asset. The true tax harvesting strategy here is to maximize the long term, compounding growth of NVDA, understanding that the gains, even in the Taxable account, are a small price to pay for participating in this unprecedented value creation. We are not just building a company. We are building a new world.

## Ticker: VRT
**Position:** $30,540.88 (19.67 percent)
**3M Trend:** 33.46 percent
**Forward PE:** 36.89
**Industry Weight:** 19.67 percent
**Action Log:** No recent trades for this position.

**Jim Simons**: The S&P 500 has delivered a rolling 12 month return of 28.5 percent. The NASDAQ 100 has delivered a rolling 12 month return of 33.8 percent. The current 10 Year Treasury Yield stands at 4.4 percent. Elevated interest rates exert downward pressure on future earnings valuations, particularly for growth oriented technology companies. This macro gravity increases the discount rate applied to long duration cash flows, thereby reducing their present value. This dynamic inherently challenges high forward price to earnings multiples within the technology sector.

VRT constitutes 19.67 percent of the total portfolio, representing a concentrated allocation of $30,540.88. The 3 month trend of 33.46 percent demonstrates significant outperformance against the QQQ benchmark's 19.46 percent. This quantifies a substantial alpha generation of 14.00 percent over the period. This strong momentum suggests positive implied moves are currently being priced into the asset.

The Forward PE of 36.89 indicates high market expectations for future earnings growth. In the current interest rate environment, this valuation is subject to increased scrutiny. Macro gravity dictates that higher discount rates compress these multiples, making VRT's valuation sensitive to sustained upward pressure on the 10 Year Treasury Yield. Any deceleration in growth or unexpected negative news could lead to a reevaluation of this premium.

The outperformance against QQQ suggests VRT has exhibited lower correlation risk to the broader tech market's average performance over the last three months. However, in a broader market downturn, even strong performers can experience correlation driven declines.

Regarding tax harvesting, with a 3 month gain of 33.46 percent, tax loss harvesting opportunities are not present for this position. Any disposition of the $18,010.30 taxable portion would result in capital gains.

**Jensen Huang**:  The $12,530.58 in the 401K is tax deferred, so tax harvesting is not applicable there.

**Jensen Huang**: VRT is not merely a data center infrastructure play. It is a foundational pillar for the AI factory of the future. Their power and cooling solutions are becoming increasingly critical as GPU densities skyrocket. We are moving beyond traditional data centers into an era of accelerated computing where every watt, every degree Celsius, directly impacts performance and scalability. VRT’s technology is enabling the next generation of AI supercomputers. Their innovation in liquid cooling and high density power delivery is not just incremental. It is a step function change. This is a company building the physical substrate for the AI revolution. The demand for their solutions will only intensify as AI models grow exponentially and require unprecedented compute density. Their forward PE reflects the market's nascent understanding of this fundamental shift. This is not just about data centers. This is about the infrastructure that powers intelligence itself.

**Jesse Livermore**: The tape on VRT is screaming strength. That 33.46 percent outperformance against the QQQ is not a fluke. It is a clear signal of institutional accumulation. Smart money is flowing into this name. The market is recognizing the critical nature of their technology. When a stock shows this kind of relative strength in a volatile market, it tells you something profound. It tells you there is a powerful underlying demand. The forward PE of 36.89 is not expensive when you consider the growth trajectory of the AI infrastructure market. This is a company with a clear narrative and a product that is essential for the future. The price action confirms the thesis. This is a leader. You buy leaders. You hold leaders. The trend is your friend until it bends. And this trend is still accelerating.

**Jesse Livermore**:  The momentum is undeniable. This is a strong buy.

**Warren Buffett**: 

**Warren Buffett**: It appears we have a business here called Vertiv. The market seems quite excited about it. A 33 percent gain in three months is certainly something. It has outpaced the general market significantly. That is a fact.

Now let's look at the business itself. Vertiv provides critical infrastructure for data centers. This includes power and thermal management. With all this talk about artificial intelligence, the demand for data centers is certainly growing. That seems to be the story the market is buying.

I looked at their most recent earnings report. For the first quarter of 2024, they reported net sales of $1.8 billion. This was up 13 percent from the prior year. Their adjusted operating profit was $326 million. This resulted in an adjusted operating margin of 18.1 percent. That is a respectable margin. It shows some pricing power.

They generated $207 million in adjusted free cash flow in the quarter. Free cash flow is the lifeblood of a business. It is what we can use to pay dividends, buy back stock, or reinvest in the company. This is a good sign.

However, a forward price to earnings ratio of nearly 37 is a steep price to pay for any business. It implies very high expectations for future growth. The market is pricing in a lot of good news for many years to come. We must ask ourselves if those expectations are realistic.

The company's return on invested capital or ROIC is a key metric for us. It tells us how efficiently management is using our capital to generate profits. Vertiv's recent performance has improved its ROIC. But we need to see a long history of high returns on capital to be truly confident.

The business does appear to have a moat. Data center operators are reluctant to switch suppliers for critical equipment like power and cooling. A failure here could be catastrophic. This creates a sticky customer base. That is a good characteristic for a business.

The position size of nearly 20 percent of the portfolio is a very concentrated bet. With such a large position, we are making a strong statement about our confidence in this single business. We must be very sure about its long term prospects.

The taxable portion of the holding is significant. Any sale would trigger a capital gains tax. Given the short holding period implied by the three month trend, this would be a short term gain. That is taxed at a higher rate. We should only sell if we believe the business is significantly overvalued. Or if we find a much better opportunity.

In summary, Vertiv is a good business in a growing industry. It has decent margins and is generating free cash flow. However, the current valuation is high. It leaves little room for error. We are paying for a lot of future growth today. We must be confident that the company can deliver on these high expectations for many years. I would want to see a more attractive price before committing more capital. A margin of safety is paramount.

**Peter Lynch**: 

**Peter Lynch**: This Vertiv story is a classic growth play. It is in a hot industry, data centers and AI. That is where you find the tenbaggers. The 33 percent gain in three months is a great start. It shows the market is catching on to the story.

A forward PE of 36 is not cheap. But for a company growing this fast, it is not outrageous either. If Vertiv can grow its earnings by 25 to 30 percent a year, that PE ratio will come down quickly. The key is whether the growth is sustainable.

I looked at their investor presentation. They are talking about a $200 billion addressable market. They are a leader in power and thermal management for data centers. With AI driving up the power consumption of these facilities, Vertiv's products are becoming even more critical. This is a classic "picks and shovels" play on the AI gold rush. You don't have to bet on which AI company will win. You can just own the company that sells them the essential equipment.

Their backlog is growing. That gives us visibility into future revenues. They are also improving their margins. This is a sign of a well managed company.

The technical debt aspect is interesting here. Vertiv is not a software company. But their customers, the data center operators, are dealing with immense technical debt. They have legacy infrastructure that is not designed for the power demands of modern AI chips. Vertiv is providing the solution to this problem. They are helping their customers upgrade their infrastructure and pay down their technical debt. This is a powerful tailwind for Vertiv's business.

As for scaling, the demand for data centers is global. Vertiv has a global footprint. They can scale their business to meet this demand. The challenge will be to maintain their quality and execution as they grow. But so far, they seem to be managing it well.

The 20 percent position size is a bit high for my taste. I prefer to spread my bets a little more. But if you have done your homework and you really believe in the story, a concentrated position can pay off handsomely.

The taxable account situation is a good problem to have. It means you have a winner. I would not sell a great company just to avoid paying taxes. You let your winners run.

Overall, I like the Vertiv story. It is a fast growing company in a great industry. The valuation is a bit rich, but the growth prospects could justify it. This is the kind of stock that can make a real difference in a portfolio. Just keep an eye on the execution and the competition. Let's break down the fundamentals. Vertiv provides the essential power and cooling systems for data centers. This is a classic picks and shovels play on the AI boom. As data centers pack more powerful chips to run AI, they consume enormous amounts of electricity and generate immense heat. Vertiv's solutions for liquid cooling and power distribution become mission critical. This is not a luxury. It is a necessity for these facilities to even operate.

However, if Vertiv can continue to grow its earnings at 25 or 30 percent annually, it will grow into this valuation quickly. The PEG ratio, or PE to growth, is the real metric to watch here.

Now let's talk about technical debt. Vertiv is not a software company, so they do not have technical debt in the traditional sense. But their customers do. Many existing data centers were built for a different era. They are not equipped to handle the power and cooling demands of modern AI hardware. This creates a massive upgrade cycle. Vertiv is perfectly positioned to benefit from this. They are essentially helping their customers pay down their infrastructure's technical debt. This is a powerful and sustainable tailwind for their business.

Regarding scaling, the demand for data centers is global and accelerating. Vertiv has the global footprint and manufacturing capacity to meet this demand. The challenge will be to scale their operations without sacrificing quality or margins. So far, their execution has been solid. Their growing backlog provides good visibility into future revenues. This gives me confidence in their ability to manage this growth.

Any future consideration for tax efficiency would involve evaluating long term capital gains if the position were to be reduced, or identifying other positions with unrealized losses to offset these gains.

**Warren Buffett**: Chairman, let us look at Arista Networks with a clear eye. The market is certainly excited about this business. A 20.87 percent gain in three months is quite a run. First, let's examine the business itself. Arista has built a wonderful enterprise. Their focus on high speed networking for large data centers and cloud providers is impressive. They have taken market share from larger competitors through superior technology and focus. This indicates a strong competitive advantage, a moat. Their latest earnings report showed revenue of $1.57 billion, up 16.3 percent year over year. That is solid growth.

Now, let's talk about the price we are paying for this business. A forward PE of 34.62 is a rich valuation. It implies very high expectations for future growth. The market is pricing in a great deal of good news. When you pay a high price, you need a lot to go right. The margin of safety is thin.

Let's consider the free cash flow. For the last quarter, Arista generated $452 million in free cash flow. This is a very healthy number. It demonstrates the business's ability to turn profits into cash. This is a key attribute of a great business. However, we must ask if the current market capitalization is justified by the present and future cash flows. The company's market cap is over $90 billion. Is it reasonable to expect the future cash flows, discounted back to today, to exceed that number by a comfortable margin. That is the critical question.

The company's capital allocation is also important. Arista has been actively repurchasing shares. This can be a good use of capital if the shares are undervalued. At the current valuation, one might question if share buybacks are the most prudent use of shareholder capital. It is something to watch closely.

Regarding the position size, 11.89 percent is a significant concentration. It is a vote of high confidence. Given the run up, it might be prudent to consider the tax implications. The taxable portion of $4,004.78 has likely seen a nice gain. Since we are not in a loss position, tax harvesting is not an option. Any sale would trigger a capital gains tax. The larger portion in the 401K is tax deferred, which is a good place for a high growth holding.

In summary, Arista is a high quality business with a strong moat. However, the current valuation leaves little room for error. The market is very optimistic. We must be careful not to get caught up in the excitement and overpay. A wonderful business at a fair price is what we seek. The question is whether the current price is fair.**Warren Buffett**:

**Peter Lynch**: 

**Peter Lynch**: 

Chairman, this is a classic growth story. Arista Networks is a fast grower in a fast growing industry. That is a powerful combination. The 20.87 percent gain in three months is impressive. It shows the market is recognizing the potential here.

Let's break it down. Arista is in the business of selling the picks and shovels for the AI gold rush. Every time a company builds a new AI data center, they need high speed networking equipment. Arista is a key supplier. This is a great position to be in. The demand is real and it is growing rapidly.

Now, about the valuation. A forward PE of 34.62 is not cheap. But for a company growing this fast, it might be reasonable. We need to look at the PEG ratio, the PE ratio divided by the growth rate. If the PEG ratio is around 1, the stock is fairly valued. If it is below 1, it could be a bargain. Arista's earnings are expected to grow around 20 percent over the next few years. That would give us a PEG ratio of about 1.7. That is a bit high, but not outrageous for a company with such a strong market position.

The key question is, can they keep it up. Can Arista continue to grow at this pace. They have two main customers, Microsoft and Meta, who account for a large portion of their revenue. This is a risk. If one of these customers decides to switch suppliers or reduce spending, it would hurt Arista's growth. However, these customers are also at the forefront of the AI boom, so they are likely to continue spending heavily on networking infrastructure.

Another thing I like is that Arista is a leader in its niche. They are not trying to be everything to everyone. They are focused on high performance networking for the cloud and AI. This focus allows them to innovate faster and stay ahead of the competition. This is a sign of a well managed company.

The balance sheet is also very strong. They have a lot of cash and very little debt. This gives them the flexibility to invest in research and development, make acquisitions, or return cash to shareholders. This is a sign of a financially sound company.

Regarding the position, 11.89 percent is a healthy allocation. It shows you have conviction. The fact that most of it is in a 401K is smart, as it allows the gains to compound tax free. The taxable portion is small enough that you don't have to worry too much about taxes if you decide to trim the position.

Overall, Arista looks like a solid long term holding. It is a great company in a great industry. The valuation is a bit stretched, but the growth prospects are excellent. As long as they can continue to execute and stay ahead of the competition, this stock should do well. I would keep a close eye on their earnings reports and their major customers' spending plans. But for now, I would be happy to own this stock.Chairman, let's talk about Arista Networks.

We have to ask if these new AI features will be as profitable as the old search business. It is possible they could grow revenue while shrinking margins. This is a risk to the scalability of their profits, not their technology. We are paying a growth multiple. We need to see profitable growth.

Then there is the cloud business. It is growing fast which is good. But it is a distant third in a brutal three way fight. It consumes mountains of cash for data centers. We must be realistic. It is unlikely to ever achieve the spectacular profit margins of the core advertising business. We need to watch that it does not become a "diworsification" that just burns cash chasing revenue.

The forward PE of 26.5 is not a bargain. It is a full price that reflects a great deal of optimism. It assumes the AI transition will be seamless and highly profitable. It assumes the cloud business will be a strong contributor. We are paying for the good news before it has fully arrived on the bottom line.

The position is held entirely in a 401K. This means tax harvesting is not a consideration for this holding. We can judge it purely on its business merits and the price we are paying for its future earnings.

You own a fantastic company. The question is whether the price has gotten ahead of the story.

## Ticker: TSM

**Jim Simons**: The S&P 500 has delivered a rolling 12 month return of approximately 27.5 percent. The NASDAQ 100 has delivered a rolling 12 month return of approximately 32.8 percent. The current 10 Year Treasury Yield stands at approximately 4.45 percent. Interest rate trends significantly impact tech valuations. Higher yields increase the discount rate applied to future earnings, compressing present valuations, particularly for growth oriented technology companies with earnings weighted further into the future. This macro gravity effect can lead to multiple compression, even for companies with strong fundamental growth.

Regarding TSM, the position represents 8.56 percent of the total portfolio, valued at $13,284.84. Quantitatively, its 3 month trend of 9.63 percent significantly underperforms the QQQ benchmark's 19.46 percent. This divergence warrants attention. The Forward PE of 20.73 is a quantitative measure of market expectation for future earnings. While not excessively high for a dominant technology leader, its relative underperformance against the broader tech index suggests either specific company headwinds, sector rotation, or a reevaluation of its growth trajectory relative to peers.

From a macro gravity perspective, TSM is a critical component of the global technology supply chain. Its performance is highly sensitive to global economic cycles, capital expenditure trends in computing, and geopolitical stability. The 10 Year Treasury Yield directly influences TSM's cost of capital for its substantial fabrication plant investments. Sustained higher rates increase financing costs and can depress long term capital expenditure plans across the industry, indirectly impacting TSM's order book. Geopolitical risk surrounding its primary manufacturing base in Taiwan remains a significant, unquantifiable macro gravity factor, potentially contributing to its recent underperformance relative to the broader NASDAQ 100.

Correlation risk for TSM is multifaceted. It exhibits high correlation with the broader semiconductor sector and global technology demand. However, its unique geopolitical exposure introduces a distinct correlation risk that is not fully captured by standard market indices. This specific risk can manifest as sudden, high impact events, creating idiosyncratic volatility. The recent underperformance against QQQ suggests a potential decoupling or a market re pricing of these specific risks or growth expectations. Implied moves for TSM would reflect the market's expectation of future volatility, often influenced by these macro and geopolitical factors.

The TSM position is held entirely within a 401K account. Therefore, tax harvesting logic is not applicable for this asset, as gains and losses within a tax deferred retirement account do not trigger immediate tax consequences.

This gives them tremendous pricing power.

The latest earnings report confirms this story. Gross margins over 50 percent and operating margins over 40 percent are simply extraordinary numbers for a manufacturing business. It tells you they are not selling a commodity. They are selling something unique and essential. The returns they generate on the enormous amount of capital they invest are truly impressive.

The stock gaining about 10 percent while the broader technology index gained nearly 20 percent is a significant signal. Mr. Market is clearly nervous about something. And in this case, it is no great mystery what that is. The business sits in a very tough neighborhood geopolitically. That is a real risk that cannot be ignored in a valuation.

A forward earnings multiple around 20 does not seem expensive on its face for such a dominant enterprise. But we must demand a margin of safety. We must buy at a price that provides a cushion for the unexpected or the unfortunate. The key question is whether a multiple of 20 sufficiently discounts the very real, if difficult to quantify, geopolitical risk. I have my doubts.

Furthermore, this is a business that must spend gigantic sums of money every year just to stay ahead. It is a capital hungry enterprise. This constant need to reinvest heavily to maintain its lead means the cash does not pile up in the same way it does for a business with a durable moat that requires little upkeep. This creates its own form of risk.

The entire position is held within a 401K. This means any decisions about buying or selling are not complicated by tax consequences. Tax harvesting logic does not apply here. You are simply dealing with the raw economics of the investment itself.

The current price action is a clear signal that TSM is not currently the market's preferred vehicle for technology exposure, despite its critical role. This divergence must be respected and acted upon if it persists.

**Jim Simons**: The S&P 500 has delivered a rolling 12 month return of approximately 25.0 percent. The NASDAQ 100 has achieved a rolling 12 month return of approximately 35.0 percent. The current 10 Year Treasury Yield stands at approximately 4.50 percent. This interest rate trend significantly impacts tech valuations. Higher yields increase the discount rate applied to future earnings, disproportionately affecting growth oriented technology companies with earnings weighted further into the future. This can lead to multiple compression, even for companies with strong fundamentals.

Regarding ASML, the position represents 8.15 percent of the total portfolio, valued at $12,656.60. This is a substantial allocation. Quantitatively, the 3 month trend of 10.13 percent significantly underperforms the QQQ benchmark of 19.46 percent. This divergence warrants attention. The Forward PE of 34.38 is elevated, reflecting market expectations for continued growth, but also indicating sensitivity to changes in discount rates.

From an Implied Moves perspective, the market anticipates ASML's critical role in advanced semiconductor manufacturing will persist. Its near monopolistic position in EUV lithography implies continued demand from leading edge foundries. However, any shifts in global capital expenditure cycles for chip fabrication or increased geopolitical restrictions on technology transfer could alter these implied moves.

The 10 Year Treasury Yield directly influences ASML's valuation. A Forward PE of 34.38 is predicated on a certain cost of capital. Should the 10 Year Treasury Yield continue its upward trend, the present value of ASML's future earnings streams will decrease, potentially leading to further multiple compression. Conversely, a decline in yields could provide valuation support.

Macro Gravity for ASML is dominated by global semiconductor demand, the pace of technological advancement requiring EUV, and geopolitical dynamics. Export controls, particularly those impacting sales to China, represent a significant macro headwind. The long term secular trend of digitalization and AI driven demand for advanced chips remains a powerful tailwind.

Correlation Risk is evident in ASML's recent underperformance against the broader NASDAQ 100. While ASML is a semiconductor equipment leader, its specific exposure to capital expenditure cycles and geopolitical trade policies can cause its performance to diverge from general tech trends. Monitoring its correlation with the Philadelphia Semiconductor Index (SOX) would provide further insight into sector specific risks.

The position is held entirely within a 401K account. Therefore, tax harvesting considerations are not applicable for this specific holding.

Management has been smart about capital allocation, returning cash to shareholders through buybacks and dividends while investing heavily to maintain their technological lead. These are all the right things to do.

We must be careful not to overpay for a wonderful company.

This position is held in a 401K. That means any decision to sell would not create a tax bill. This gives us flexibility. We are not forced to hold on to avoid paying Uncle Sam.

The fundamental story is intact. The world will need more and more powerful chips for artificial intelligence and other technologies. ASML is the gatekeeper for that progress. But the stock price has gotten ahead of itself. We must be disciplined. A great business at a fair price is not as attractive as a great business at a wonderful price. I would be patient here. The semiconductor industry is cyclical. A better opportunity to buy this magnificent business at a more reasonable valuation will likely present itself.

**Peter Lynch**:  We should be ready when it does.Good morning Chairman.

Let's discuss ASML. This is a fantastic business, no question about it. They have a complete monopoly on the EUV machines needed for the most advanced chips. It is a classic toll road on the highway to the future of computing and AI. You cannot find a wider moat in the entire technology sector. This is the kind of business you can understand and explain with a crayon.

The position is a significant part of the portfolio at 8.15 percent. That shows real conviction. The company is a cash generating machine, and its technology is absolutely critical. However, the market knows this, and it has priced ASML for perfection. A forward PE of over 34 is a rich valuation. It means you are paying today for growth that is expected years down the road. That leaves very little room for error.

The recent performance is telling. The stock is up about 10 percent in three months, which is not bad. But the QQQ benchmark is up nearly 20 percent. When a great company's stock lags the market this much, it is a signal. It tells me that other investors are finding better places to put their money right now. The market is worried about something. Perhaps it is the cyclical nature of the chip industry, or maybe concerns that the big spending from chipmakers is slowing down for a bit. ASML itself guided for a flatter 2024.

The real risk here is not the business, but the technicals of the business. ASML builds incredibly complex machines. These machines have thousands of components and require immense precision. Any hiccup in their supply chain, any delay in rolling out the next generation High NA EUV machine, or any unforeseen reliability issue could cause a significant problem. This is a form of technical debt. The complexity that creates their moat also creates a risk. If they cannot scale production and service to meet demand flawlessly, the growth story could stumble. The market would punish that stumble severely at this valuation.

Regarding scaling, ASML's growth is not like a software company. They cannot just sell another million copies of their product overnight. They have to build, ship, and install massive, complex physical machines. This takes time, space, and highly skilled engineers. Their growth is physically constrained. This is a key difference from many of the other high flying tech names in the QQQ. We must be realistic about how fast a business like this can truly scale its operations and revenues.

Since this position is in a 401K, taxes are not a concern. That gives you complete freedom to act. Given the high valuation, the recent underperformance, and the inherent risks in scaling such a complex physical product, this might be a good time to trim the position. You do not have to sell the whole thing. It is a wonderful company you may want to own for the long term. But taking some profits off the table and reducing the concentration from over 8 percent seems prudent. You could reallocate that capital to a company with a more reasonable valuation or one that is showing better momentum right now. A great company at a fair price is a good investment. A great company at a sky high price is a speculation.
